{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_016ibnMWCAC1gJdJ4vmAi16W","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01FEoG3WQqKAU2qCxcpYwPU4","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# VS Code Diagnostic API Reference\n\n## Overview\n\nThe Diagnostic API allows extensions to report code issues (errors, warnings, information, hints) to users within the VS Code editor. Diagnostics are organized into collections that extensions manage independently. The API provides a way to:\n\n- Create and manage diagnostic collections for organizing diagnostics\n- Define diagnostics with severity levels, messages, and optional code references\n- Associate related information with diagnostics to point to related code locations\n- Subscribe to global diagnostic changes\n- Retrieve diagnostics programmatically\n\nDiagnostics are scoped to a URI (file path) and managed through a `DiagnosticCollection`. All diagnostics from a collection are automatically associated with the collection's name (e.g., 'typescript', 'eslint'), which is used by the task framework for problem matchers.\n\n---\n\n## Core Types\n\n### Diagnostic\n\n**Class** that represents a single diagnostic issue in a file.\n\n#### Constructor\n```typescript\nnew Diagnostic(\n  range: Range,\n  message: string,\n  severity?: DiagnosticSeverity\n)\n```\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `range: Range` - **Required**. The range in the document where the diagnostic applies. This determines the visual location in the editor where the issue is highlighted.\n- `message: string` - **Required**. A human-readable message describing the issue.\n- `severity?: DiagnosticSeverity` - **Optional**. The severity level. Defaults to `DiagnosticSeverity.Error` if not specified.\n\n#### Properties\n\n| Property | Type | Description |\n|----------|------|-------------|\n| `range` | `Range` | The range to which this diagnostic applies. This is mutable and can be updated after creation. |\n| `message` | `string` | The human-readable message. This is mutable. |\n| `severity` | `DiagnosticSeverity` | The severity (Error, Warning, Information, Hint). Default is Error. This is mutable. |\n| `source?` | `string` | Optional. A human-readable string describing the source of this diagnostic, e.g., 'typescript', 'eslint', 'super lint'. Shown in the UI to help users identify the diagnostic source. |\n| `code?` | `string \\| number \\| { value: string \\| number; target: Uri }` | Optional. A code or identifier for this diagnostic. When used in code actions, this code can be referenced via `CodeActionContext.diagnostics`. Can be a simple value or an object with a target URI for linking to more information. |\n| `relatedInformation?` | `DiagnosticRelatedInformation[]` | Optional. An array of related diagnostic information. Used to point to code locations that cause or relate to this diagnostic, e.g., when symbol names collide in a scope. |\n| `tags?` | `DiagnosticTag[]` | Optional. Additional metadata tags (e.g., Unnecessary, Deprecated) that influence how the diagnostic is rendered in the editor. |\n\n#### Behavior Notes\n\n- **Immutability of returned diagnostics**: When retrieving diagnostics via `DiagnosticCollection.get()`, the returned array is immutable and cannot be modified. To change diagnostics, you must call `set()` again.\n- **Range precision**: The range determines exact visual highlighting. Small ranges highlight specific tokens; large ranges highlight entire sections.\n- **Severity ordering**: The editor prioritizes display based on severity (Error > Warning > Information > Hint). With very large diagnostic counts, less severe diagnostics may be hidden.\n- **Code linking**: If `code` is an object with a `target` URI, users can click it to navigate to more information, typically in extension documentation or web pages.\n\n#### Example\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nconst range = new vscode.Range(\n  new vscode.Position(0, 0),\n  new vscode.Position(0, 5)\n);\nconst diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n  range,\n  'Unused variable',\n  vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning\n);\ndiagnostic.source = 'eslint';\ndiagnostic.code = 'no-unused-vars';\ndiagnostic.tags = [vscode.DiagnosticTag.Unnecessary];\n```\n\n---\n\n### DiagnosticCollection\n\n**Interface** that acts as a container for managing diagnostics across documents. It provides methods to set, retrieve, and manage diagnostics keyed by URI.\n\n#### Constructor\n\n`DiagnosticCollection` cannot be instantiated directly. Instead, use `languages.createDiagnosticCollection()`.\n\n#### Properties\n\n| Property | Type | Description |\n|----------|------|-------------|\n| `name` | `string` (readonly) | The name of this collection. Every diagnostic from this collection is associated with this name. Used by the task framework for problem matcher integration. Examples: 'typescript', 'eslint', 'myLinter'. |\n\n#### Methods\n\n##### `set(uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined): void`\n\nAssign diagnostics for a given resource, replacing any existing diagnostics for that resource.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri: Uri` - The resource identifier (file path).\n- `diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined` - Array of diagnostics, or `undefined` to clear all diagnostics for this URI.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Passing `undefined` is equivalent to calling `delete(uri)`.\n- Multiple calls to `set()` with the same URI will replace all previous diagnostics for that URI.\n- Diagnostics are stored immutably; the array is copied internally.\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n  range,\n  'Error message',\n  vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n);\ncollection.set(document.uri, [diagnostic]);\n\n// Clear diagnostics for this file\ncollection.set(document.uri, undefined);\n```\n\n##### `set(entries: ReadonlyArray<[Uri, readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined]>): void`\n\nReplace diagnostics for multiple resources in a single call.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `entries` - An array of `[Uri, Diagnostic[]]` tuples.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Multiple tuples with the same URI are merged (combined), e.g., `[[file1, [d1]], [file1, [d2]]]` becomes `[[file1, [d1, d2]]]`.\n- If an entry has `undefined` as diagnostics, all previous diagnostics for that URI are removed (but later entries for the same URI are still processed).\n- This is more efficient than multiple `set()` calls when updating many files.\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst entries: [vscode.Uri, vscode.Diagnostic[]][] = [\n  [file1Uri, [diag1, diag2]],\n  [file2Uri, [diag3]],\n  [file3Uri, undefined] // Clear file3\n];\ncollection.set(entries);\n```\n\n##### `delete(uri: Uri): void`\n\nRemove all diagnostics for a given resource.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri: Uri` - The resource identifier.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Equivalent to calling `set(uri, undefined)`.\n- Does nothing if the URI has no diagnostics.\n\n##### `clear(): void`\n\nRemove all diagnostics from this collection across all resources.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Fires the `onDidChangeDiagnostics` event with all affected URIs.\n\n##### `forEach(callback: (uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[], collection: DiagnosticCollection) => any, thisArg?: any): void`\n\nIterate over each entry in the collection.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `callback` - Function called for each URI/diagnostics pair.\n- `thisArg` - Optional `this` context for the callback.\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\ncollection.forEach((uri, diagnostics, col) => {\n  console.log(`${uri.path}: ${diagnostics.length} diagnostics`);\n});\n```\n\n##### `get(uri: Uri): readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined`\n\nGet the diagnostics for a given resource.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri: Uri` - The resource identifier.\n\n**Returns:**\n- An immutable array of diagnostics, or `undefined` if the URI has no diagnostics.\n\n**Important:** The returned array is immutable and cannot be modified. To update diagnostics, call `set()` with a new array.\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnostics = collection.get(document.uri);\nif (diagnostics) {\n  console.log(`Found ${diagnostics.length} diagnostics`);\n}\n```\n\n##### `has(uri: Uri): boolean`\n\nCheck if this collection contains diagnostics for a given resource.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri: Uri` - The resource identifier.\n\n**Returns:**\n- `true` if the collection has any diagnostics for the URI, `false` otherwise.\n\n##### `dispose(): void`\n\nDispose and free associated resources. Clears all diagnostics from the collection.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Calls `clear()` internally.\n- The collection becomes unusable after disposal.\n- Typically called during extension deactivation.\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('myLinter');\n// ... use collection ...\ncollection.dispose(); // Clean up on extension deactivation\n```\n\n#### Iterable Support\n\n`DiagnosticCollection` implements `Iterable<[uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[]]>`, allowing it to be used with `for...of`:\n\n```typescript\nfor (const [uri, diagnostics] of collection) {\n  console.log(`${uri.path}: ${diagnostics.length} issues`);\n}\n```\n\n#### Behavior Notes\n\n- **Cardinality limits**: VS Code has a maximum of 1000 diagnostics per file. If more are provided, only the highest-severity diagnostics are kept, with lower-severity diagnostics removed. The global limit is approximately 1100 diagnostics per file across all collections.\n- **Immutability**: Once a diagnostic array is set, the internal copy is immutable. Modifying the original array after calling `set()` has no effect.\n- **URI equivalence**: URIs are compared by their string representation. URIs with identical components but different representations may be treated as different.\n\n---\n\n### DiagnosticSeverity\n\n**Enum** that defines the severity levels for diagnostics.\n\n```typescript\nexport enum DiagnosticSeverity {\n  Error = 0,\n  Warning = 1,\n  Information = 2,\n  Hint = 3\n}\n```\n\n#### Members\n\n| Member | Value | Description |\n|--------|-------|-------------|\n| `Error` | `0` | Something not allowed by the rules of a language or other means. Shown with red squiggle. Highest priority. |\n| `Warning` | `1` | Something suspicious but allowed. Shown with orange/yellow squiggle. |\n| `Information` | `2` | Something to inform about but not a problem. Shown with blue squiggle. |\n| `Hint` | `3` | Something to hint at a better way of doing it, like proposing a refactoring. Shown with green squiggle or lightbulb. Lowest priority. |\n\n#### Usage Notes\n\n- **Default severity**: If not specified, `Diagnostic` defaults to `Error`.\n- **Display priority**: When the editor has space constraints, higher-severity diagnostics are shown first.\n- **Visual rendering**: Each severity has associated colors configured via VS Code's theme.\n\n#### Example\n```typescript\nconst errorDiag = new vscode.Diagnostic(range, 'Critical error', vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error);\nconst warnDiag = new vscode.Diagnostic(range, 'Potential issue', vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning);\nconst infoDiag = new vscode.Diagnostic(range, 'FYI', vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Information);\nconst hintDiag = new vscode.Diagnostic(range, 'Try this instead', vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Hint);\n```\n\n---\n\n### DiagnosticRelatedInformation\n\n**Class** representing additional context for a diagnostic, pointing to related code locations.\n\n#### Constructor\n```typescript\nnew DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n  location: Location,\n  message: string\n)\n```\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `location: Location` - **Required**. The location in code that relates to the diagnostic. Includes both a URI and a range.\n- `message: string` - **Required**. A human-readable message describing the relationship.\n\n#### Properties\n\n| Property | Type | Description |\n|----------|------|-------------|\n| `location` | `Location` | The location (URI + range) of this related information. |\n| `message` | `string` | A human-readable message explaining the relationship. |\n\n#### Use Cases\n\n- **Duplicate symbols**: When a symbol name collides in a scope, mark all definitions.\n- **Multi-location issues**: Point to multiple locations that together form a problem.\n- **Related errors**: Show related errors or warnings in other files.\n\n#### Example\n```typescript\nconst diag = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n  range,\n  'Duplicate symbol name',\n  vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n);\n\n// Link to the first occurrence of the symbol\ndiag.relatedInformation = [\n  new vscode.DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n    new vscode.Location(file1Uri, otherRange),\n    'First defined here'\n  ),\n  new vscode.DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n    new vscode.Location(file2Uri, anotherRange),\n    'Also defined here'\n  )\n];\n```\n\n#### Behavior Notes\n\n- **UI rendering**: VS Code displays related information as links in the Problems panel and hover tooltips.\n- **Navigation**: Clicking a related information link navigates to that location.\n\n---\n\n### DiagnosticTag\n\n**Enum** providing metadata about diagnostic types that influence rendering.\n\n```typescript\nexport enum DiagnosticTag {\n  Unnecessary = 1,\n  Deprecated = 2\n}\n```\n\n#### Members\n\n| Member | Value | Description |\n|--------|-------|-------------|\n| `Unnecessary` | `1` | Marks unused or unnecessary code. Rendered faded out (opacity controlled by `editorUnnecessaryCode.opacity` theme color). In high-contrast themes, uses `editorUnnecessaryCode.border` to underline instead. |\n| `Deprecated` | `2` | Marks deprecated or obsolete code. Rendered with a strike-through effect. |\n\n#### Theme Color Configuration\n\n**For `Unnecessary` tag:**\n```json\n{\n  \"editorUnnecessaryCode.opacity\": \"#000000c0\",  // 75% opacity\n  \"editorUnnecessaryCode.border\": \"#ff0000\"      // Red underline in high contrast\n}\n```\n\n#### Usage Notes\n\n- **Visual feedback**: Tags provide visual cues beyond severity color. Multiple tags can be applied to a single diagnostic.\n- **User intent**: These tags communicate intent more precisely than severity alone (e.g., a warning about unused code is more specific than generic warning).\n\n#### Example\n```typescript\nconst diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n  range,\n  'Unused variable `x`',\n  vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Information\n);\ndiagnostic.tags = [vscode.DiagnosticTag.Unnecessary];\n\nconst deprecated = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n  range,\n  'This API is deprecated',\n  vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning\n);\ndeprecated.tags = [vscode.DiagnosticTag.Deprecated];\n```\n\n---\n\n## Functions\n\n### createDiagnosticCollection()\n\nFactory function to create a new `DiagnosticCollection`.\n\n#### Signature\n```typescript\nexport function createDiagnosticCollection(name?: string): DiagnosticCollection\n```\n\n#### Parameters\n\n- `name?: string` - **Optional**. The name of the collection. If not provided, a unique auto-generated name is used. The name is associated with all diagnostics in the collection and is used by the task framework for problem matcher integration.\n\n#### Returns\n\nA new `DiagnosticCollection` instance.\n\n#### Behavior Notes\n\n- **Ownership**: The returned collection is owned by the extension. The extension is responsible for populating and disposing of it.\n- **Uniqueness**: Each call returns a new, independent collection. Collections with the same name are distinct objects.\n- **Task framework integration**: If you want problem matchers to recognize your diagnostics, use a consistent name (e.g., 'myLinter', 'typescript').\n- **Resource lifecycle**: The collection persists until explicitly disposed.\n\n#### Example\n```typescript\nconst collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('myLinter');\n\n// Later, set diagnostics\nconst diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(range, 'Issue found');\ncollection.set(document.uri, [diagnostic]);\n\n// On deactivation, clean up\nvscode.workspace.onDidChangeConfiguration(() => {\n  collection.clear();\n});\n\n// In extension deactivate()\nexport function deactivate() {\n  collection.dispose();\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### getDiagnostics()\n\nRetrieve diagnostics from the workspace.\n\n#### Overload 1: Get diagnostics for a specific resource\n```typescript\nexport function getDiagnostics(resource: Uri): Diagnostic[]\n```\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `resource: Uri` - The resource (file path) to get diagnostics for.\n\n**Returns:**\n- An array of all diagnostics for that resource across all collections, or an empty array if none.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns diagnostics from all diagnostic collections (both built-in and extension-created).\n- Does not include only the diagnostics from a single collection; this is a global query.\n\n#### Overload 2: Get all diagnostics\n```typescript\nexport function getDiagnostics(): [Uri, Diagnostic[]][]\n```\n\n**Parameters:** None\n\n**Returns:**\n- An array of `[Uri, Diagnostic[]]` tuples representing all diagnostics in the workspace across all collections.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns a snapshot of diagnostics at the time of the call.\n- Does not include URIs with zero diagnostics.\n\n#### Example\n```typescript\n// Get diagnostics for a specific file\nconst fileDiags = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(document.uri);\nconsole.log(`File has ${fileDiags.length} diagnostics`);\n\n// Get all diagnostics in the workspace\nconst allDiags = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics();\nlet totalDiagCount = 0;\nfor (const [uri, diags] of allDiags) {\n  console.log(`${uri.path}: ${diags.length}`);\n  totalDiagCount += diags.length;\n}\nconsole.log(`Total: ${totalDiagCount}`);\n```\n\n#### Behavior Notes\n\n- **Aggregation**: Results include diagnostics from all sources (language servers, linters, type checkers, etc.).\n- **Immutability**: The returned arrays are read-only and cannot be modified.\n- **Performance**: Retrieving all diagnostics in a large workspace can be expensive. Filter by URI when possible.\n\n---\n\n## Events\n\n### onDidChangeDiagnostics\n\n**Event** fired when the global set of diagnostics changes (new or removed diagnostics).\n\n#### Signature\n```typescript\nexport const onDidChangeDiagnostics: Event<DiagnosticChangeEvent>\n```\n\n#### DiagnosticChangeEvent Interface\n```typescript\nexport interface DiagnosticChangeEvent {\n  readonly uris: readonly Uri[];\n}\n```\n\n**Properties:**\n- `uris: readonly Uri[]` - An array of URIs for which diagnostics have changed (either added, modified, or removed).\n\n#### Subscription\n```typescript\nexport interface Event<T> {\n  (listener: (e: T) => any, thisArgs?: any, disposables?: Disposable[]): Disposable\n}\n```\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `listener` - Callback function invoked when diagnostics change.\n- `thisArgs` - Optional `this` context for the callback.\n- `disposables` - Optional array to which an unsubscribe disposable will be added.\n\n**Returns:** A `Disposable` that unsubscribes the listener when disposed.\n\n#### When the Event Fires\n\n- When any extension's `DiagnosticCollection.set()` is called.\n- When an extension's collection is `clear()`d or `dispose()`d.\n- When a collection's diagnostics are replaced with `set(entries)`.\n- When a specific resource's diagnostics are `delete()`d.\n\n#### Important Notes\n\n- **Batching**: The event may be debounced (delayed) if many changes occur in quick succession, batching them together for efficiency.\n- **URI list only**: The event provides the list of changed URIs but not the actual diagnostics. To inspect diagnostics, call `getDiagnostics()`.\n- **Performance**: Do not perform expensive operations directly in the listener; schedule async work instead.\n\n#### Example\n```typescript\nconst disposable = vscode.languages.onDidChangeDiagnostics((event) => {\n  console.log(`Diagnostics changed for ${event.uris.length} URIs`);\n\n  for (const uri of event.uris) {\n    const diags = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(uri);\n    console.log(`${uri.path}: ${diags.length} diagnostics`);\n\n    // Filter and process\n    const errors = diags.filter(d => d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error);\n    console.log(`  Errors: ${errors.length}`);\n  }\n});\n\n// Later, unsubscribe\ndisposable.dispose();\n```\n\n#### Cleanup\n\nThe listener is automatically cleaned up when:\n1. The returned `Disposable` is disposed.\n2. The extension is deactivated.\n\nIt's good practice to return the disposable from `activate()` or add it to a disposables list:\n```typescript\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n  context.subscriptions.push(\n    vscode.languages.onDidChangeDiagnostics(handler)\n  );\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Usage Examples\n\n### Basic Example: Creating and Publishing Diagnostics\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n  // Create a diagnostic collection\n  const diagnostics = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('myLinter');\n  context.subscriptions.push(diagnostics);\n\n  // Listen for text document changes\n  vscode.workspace.onDidOpenTextDocument((document) => {\n    lintDocument(document, diagnostics);\n  });\n\n  vscode.workspace.onDidChangeTextDocument((event) => {\n    lintDocument(event.document, diagnostics);\n  });\n\n  vscode.workspace.onDidCloseTextDocument((document) => {\n    // Clear diagnostics when document is closed\n    diagnostics.delete(document.uri);\n  });\n\n  // Lint existing documents\n  vscode.workspace.textDocuments.forEach((document) => {\n    lintDocument(document, diagnostics);\n  });\n}\n\nfunction lintDocument(\n  document: vscode.TextDocument,\n  diagnostics: vscode.DiagnosticCollection\n) {\n  const issues: vscode.Diagnostic[] = [];\n\n  // Simple example: flag lines longer than 120 characters\n  for (let i = 0; i < document.lineCount; i++) {\n    const line = document.lineAt(i);\n    if (line.text.length > 120) {\n      const range = new vscode.Range(\n        new vscode.Position(i, 120),\n        new vscode.Position(i, line.text.length)\n      );\n      const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n        range,\n        'Line exceeds 120 characters',\n        vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning\n      );\n      diagnostic.source = 'myLinter';\n      diagnostic.code = 'line-length';\n      issues.push(diagnostic);\n    }\n  }\n\n  // Publish all diagnostics for this document\n  diagnostics.set(document.uri, issues);\n}\n\nexport function deactivate() {\n  // Clean up is handled by context.subscriptions\n}\n```\n\n### Advanced Example: Multiple Files with Related Information\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n  const diagnostics = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('analyzer');\n  context.subscriptions.push(diagnostics);\n\n  const analyzeWorkspace = async () => {\n    // Find all duplicate symbol definitions\n    const allSymbols = await findAllSymbols();\n    const duplicates = findDuplicates(allSymbols);\n\n    // Create diagnostics for each duplicate\n    const entries: [vscode.Uri, vscode.Diagnostic[]][] = [];\n\n    for (const [symbolName, locations] of duplicates) {\n      for (let i = 0; i < locations.length; i++) {\n        const location = locations[i];\n        const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n          location.range,\n          `Duplicate symbol: '${symbolName}' is defined ${locations.length} times`,\n          vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n        );\n        diagnostic.source = 'analyzer';\n        diagnostic.code = { value: 'duplicate-symbol', target: vscode.Uri.parse('https://docs.example.com/rules/duplicate-symbol') };\n\n        // Link to all other definitions\n        diagnostic.relatedInformation = locations\n          .map((loc, idx) => idx !== i ? loc : null)\n          .filter(Boolean)\n          .map((loc) => new vscode.DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n            loc,\n            `Other definition of '${symbolName}'`\n          ));\n\n        entries.push([location.uri, [diagnostic]]);\n      }\n    }\n\n    // Set all diagnostics at once\n    diagnostics.set(entries);\n  };\n\n  // Re-analyze when configuration changes\n  context.subscriptions.push(\n    vscode.workspace.onDidChangeConfiguration(() => {\n      analyzeWorkspace();\n    })\n  );\n\n  // Initial analysis\n  analyzeWorkspace();\n}\n\nasync function findAllSymbols(): Promise<Map<string, vscode.Location[]>> {\n  // Implementation omitted\n  return new Map();\n}\n\nfunction findDuplicates(\n  symbols: Map<string, vscode.Location[]>\n): Map<string, vscode.Location[]> {\n  const duplicates = new Map<string, vscode.Location[]>();\n  for (const [name, locations] of symbols) {\n    if (locations.length > 1) {\n      duplicates.set(name, locations);\n    }\n  }\n  return duplicates;\n}\n```\n\n### Example: Monitoring Diagnostic Changes\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n  // Monitor when diagnostics change globally\n  const listener = vscode.languages.onDidChangeDiagnostics((event) => {\n    console.log('Diagnostics changed!');\n    console.log(`Modified URIs: ${event.uris.length}`);\n\n    // Count errors and warnings\n    let totalErrors = 0;\n    let totalWarnings = 0;\n\n    for (const uri of event.uris) {\n      const diags = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(uri);\n      for (const diag of diags) {\n        if (diag.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error) {\n          totalErrors++;\n        } else if (diag.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning) {\n          totalWarnings++;\n        }\n      }\n    }\n\n    console.log(`Total errors: ${totalErrors}, warnings: ${totalWarnings}`);\n\n    // Update status bar\n    if (totalErrors > 0) {\n      vscode.window.setStatusBarMessage(`$(error) ${totalErrors} errors`);\n    } else if (totalWarnings > 0) {\n      vscode.window.setStatusBarMessage(`$(warning) ${totalWarnings} warnings`);\n    }\n  });\n\n  context.subscriptions.push(listener);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Common Patterns\n\n### Pattern 1: Batch Updating Multiple Files\n\nInstead of calling `set()` multiple times, batch updates for better performance:\n\n```typescript\n// ❌ Inefficient: Multiple calls\ndiagnostics.set(file1, diags1);\ndiagnostics.set(file2, diags2);\ndiagnostics.set(file3, diags3);\n\n// ✅ Efficient: Batch call\ndiagnostics.set([\n  [file1, diags1],\n  [file2, diags2],\n  [file3, diags3],\n]);\n```\n\n### Pattern 2: Clearing Diagnostics\n\n```typescript\n// Option 1: Clear specific file\ndiagnostics.delete(uri);\n\n// Option 2: Clear all with undefined\ndiagnostics.set(uri, undefined);\n\n// Option 3: Clear entire collection\ndiagnostics.clear();\n```\n\n### Pattern 3: Code Actions Linked to Diagnostics\n\nUse the `code` property to connect diagnostics to code actions:\n\n```typescript\n// In your linter\nconst diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(range, 'Use const instead of let');\ndiagnostic.code = { value: 'prefer-const', target: vscode.Uri.parse('https://...') };\n\n// In your code action provider\nvscode.languages.registerCodeActionProvider('javascript', {\n  provideCodeActions(document, range, context) {\n    return context.diagnostics\n      .filter(d => d.code?.value === 'prefer-const')\n      .map(d => {\n        const action = new vscode.CodeAction('Use const', vscode.CodeActionKind.QuickFix);\n        action.edit = new vscode.WorkspaceEdit();\n        action.edit.replace(document.uri, d.range, 'const');\n        return action;\n      });\n  }\n});\n```\n\n### Pattern 4: Filtering and Querying Diagnostics\n\n```typescript\n// Get all errors in current document\nconst errors = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(editor.document.uri)\n  .filter(d => d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error);\n\n// Get all diagnostics from a specific source\nconst tsDiagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics()\n  .flatMap(([uri, diags]) => diags.filter(d => d.source === 'typescript'))\n  .map(d => d);\n\n// Count diagnostics by severity\nconst summary = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics().reduce(\n  (acc, [_uri, diags]) => {\n    for (const d of diags) {\n      acc[d.severity] = (acc[d.severity] || 0) + 1;\n    }\n    return acc;\n  },\n  {} as Record<number, number>\n);\n```\n\n### Pattern 5: Document-Scoped Diagnostics\n\nIf your extension only cares about the active document:\n\n```typescript\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n  const diagnostics = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('myLinter');\n  context.subscriptions.push(diagnostics);\n\n  let lastDocument: vscode.TextDocument | undefined;\n\n  const lint = (document: vscode.TextDocument) => {\n    if (lastDocument && lastDocument !== document) {\n      // Clear diagnostics from the previous document\n      diagnostics.delete(lastDocument.uri);\n    }\n    lastDocument = document;\n\n    const issues = performLinting(document);\n    diagnostics.set(document.uri, issues);\n  };\n\n  if (vscode.window.activeTextEditor) {\n    lint(vscode.window.activeTextEditor.document);\n  }\n\n  context.subscriptions.push(\n    vscode.window.onDidChangeActiveTextEditor((editor) => {\n      if (editor) lint(editor.document);\n    }),\n    vscode.workspace.onDidChangeTextDocument((event) => {\n      if (event.document === vscode.window.activeTextEditor?.document) {\n        lint(event.document);\n      }\n    })\n  );\n}\n\nfunction performLinting(document: vscode.TextDocument): vscode.Diagnostic[] {\n  // Your linting logic here\n  return [];\n}\n```\n\n### Pattern 6: Debouncing Diagnostic Updates\n\nFor performance, debounce frequent updates:\n\n```typescript\nimport { throttle } from 'lodash'; // or implement your own\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n  const diagnostics = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('myLinter');\n  context.subscriptions.push(diagnostics);\n\n  const debouncedLint = throttle((document: vscode.TextDocument) => {\n    const issues = performLinting(document);\n    diagnostics.set(document.uri, issues);\n  }, 500); // Update at most every 500ms\n\n  context.subscriptions.push(\n    vscode.workspace.onDidChangeTextDocument((event) => {\n      debouncedLint(event.document);\n    })\n  );\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Common Error Scenarios\n\n#### 1. Setting Diagnostics on Non-Existent URI\n\n```typescript\n// This doesn't cause an error, but the diagnostics are stored\n// and will appear if the file is ever opened\ndiagnostics.set(vscode.Uri.parse('file:///does/not/exist.js'), [diagnostic]);\n```\n\n#### 2. Disposed Collection\n\nAttempting to use a disposed `DiagnosticCollection` throws an error:\n\n```typescript\nconst col = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('test');\ncol.dispose();\n\ncol.set(uri, [diagnostic]); // ❌ Throws: Collection is disposed\n```\n\n**Prevention:**\n```typescript\nconst disposables: vscode.Disposable[] = [];\nconst col = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('test');\ndisposables.push(col);\n\nexport function deactivate() {\n  disposables.forEach(d => d.dispose());\n}\n```\n\n#### 3. Modifying Returned Diagnostic Array\n\n```typescript\nconst diags = collection.get(uri); // Returns immutable array\ndiags[0].message = 'New message'; // ❌ Change is not reflected\n\n// ✅ Correct approach:\nconst updated = diags.map(d => {\n  if (d === diags[0]) {\n    const newDiag = new vscode.Diagnostic(d.range, 'New message', d.severity);\n    newDiag.source = d.source;\n    return newDiag;\n  }\n  return d;\n});\ncollection.set(uri, updated);\n```\n\n#### 4. Diagnostic Count Limits\n\nVS Code limits diagnostics per file to prevent performance degradation:\n\n```typescript\n// If you set more than ~1000 diagnostics per file,\n// only the highest-severity ones are retained\nconst tooMany = Array.from({ length: 2000 }, (_, i) =>\n  new vscode.Diagnostic(\n    new vscode.Range(i, 0, i, 1),\n    'Issue',\n    vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Hint\n  )\n);\n\ndiagnostics.set(uri, tooMany); // Only ~1000 stored (highest severity prioritized)\n```\n\n**Best practice:** Don't generate excessive diagnostics. Consider aggregating or sampling them.\n\n#### 5. Missing Required Properties\n\n```typescript\n// ❌ Invalid: missing range\nconst bad = new vscode.Diagnostic(null, 'message'); // TypeScript error\n\n// ❌ Invalid: missing message\nconst bad2 = new vscode.Diagnostic(range, ''); // Empty string is allowed but not useful\n\n// ✅ Valid: minimal required properties\nconst good = new vscode.Diagnostic(range, 'message');\n```\n\n### Defensive Programming Practices\n\n```typescript\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n  const diagnostics = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('myLinter');\n  context.subscriptions.push(diagnostics);\n\n  const safeLint = async (document: vscode.TextDocument) => {\n    try {\n      if (!document.uri.fsPath.endsWith('.myLang')) {\n        return; // Skip non-relevant files\n      }\n\n      const issues = await performLinting(document);\n\n      // Validate diagnostics before setting\n      const valid = issues.filter(d => {\n        if (!d.range || !d.message) {\n          console.warn('Invalid diagnostic, skipping:', d);\n          return false;\n        }\n        return true;\n      });\n\n      diagnostics.set(document.uri, valid);\n    } catch (error) {\n      console.error('Linting failed:', error);\n      // Optionally set an error diagnostic\n      const errorDiag = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n        new vscode.Range(0, 0, 0, 0),\n        `Linting error: ${String(error)}`,\n        vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n      );\n      diagnostics.set(document.uri, [errorDiag]);\n    }\n  };\n\n  context.subscriptions.push(\n    vscode.workspace.onDidChangeTextDocument((event) => {\n      safeLint(event.document).catch(console.error);\n    })\n  );\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Real-World Patterns from VS Code Extensions\n\n### Pattern from TypeScript Extension\n\nThe TypeScript extension maps TypeScript diagnostics to VS Code diagnostics, preserving diagnostic codes and related information:\n\n```typescript\nconst typeScriptDiagnostic = serverDiagnostic;\nconst vscDiagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n  serverDiagnostic.range,\n  serverDiagnostic.message,\n  mapSeverity(serverDiagnostic.category)\n);\nvscDiagnostic.source = 'typescript';\nvscDiagnostic.code = serverDiagnostic.code;\n\nif (serverDiagnostic.relatedInformation) {\n  vscDiagnostic.relatedInformation = serverDiagnostic.relatedInformation\n    .map(info => new vscode.DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n      new vscode.Location(info.file, info.range),\n      info.message\n    ));\n}\n```\n\n### Pattern from Extension-Editing Extension\n\nThe built-in Extension Editing extension validates `package.json` files and uses diagnostic codes with links:\n\n```typescript\nconst diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n  range,\n  'Unsafe activation event',\n  vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n);\ndiagnostic.code = {\n  value: 'unsafe-activation-event',\n  target: vscode.Uri.parse('https://code.visualstudio.com/api/references/activation-events')\n};\n```\n\nThis pattern allows users to click the diagnostic code to learn more.\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe VS Code Diagnostic API provides a robust system for reporting code issues to users. Key takeaways:\n\n1. **Collections** organize diagnostics and associate them with a source name.\n2. **Severity** determines visual priority and how diagnostics are displayed.\n3. **Related information** provides additional context by linking to related code locations.\n4. **Tags** (Unnecessary, Deprecated) provide visual and semantic hints about diagnostic types.\n5. **Events** allow extensions to react to diagnostic changes globally.\n6. **Batch operations** improve performance when updating many files.\n7. **Proper cleanup** via `dispose()` is essential for extension health.\n\nUse this API to provide timely, contextual feedback to developers about code quality, style, and correctness issues within VS Code.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1303,"cache_read_input_tokens":75907,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1303},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"11f8bcf2-3366-441e-a54f-481f5244895a","uuid":"3890778b-a5ed-4a5d-bad4-8fd99e05bbb3"}

Diagnostics are organized into collections that extensions manage independently. The API provides a way to:\n\n- Create and manage diagnostic collections for organizing diagnostics\n- Define diagnostics with severity levels, messages, and optional code references\n- Associate related information with diagnostics to point to related code locations\n- Subscribe to global diagnostic changes\n- Retrieve diagnostics programmatically\n\nDiagnostics are scoped to a URI (file path) and managed through a `DiagnosticCollection`. All diagnostics from a collection are automatically associated with the collection's name (e.g., 'typescript', 'eslint'), which is used by the task framework for problem matchers.\n\n---\n\n## Core Types\n\n### Diagnostic\n\n**Class** that represents a single diagnostic issue in a file.\n\n#### Constructor\n```typescript\nnew Diagnostic(\n  range: Range,\n  message: string,\n  severity?: DiagnosticSeverity\n)\n```\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `range: Range` - **Required**. The range in the document where the diagnostic applies. This determines the visual location in the editor where the issue is highlighted.\n- `message: string` - **Required**. A human-readable message describing the issue.\n- `severity?: DiagnosticSeverity` - **Optional**. The severity level. Defaults to `DiagnosticSeverity.Error` if not specified.\n\n#### Properties\n\n| Property | Type | Description |\n|----------|------|-------------|\n| `range` | `Range` | The range to which this diagnostic applies. This is mutable and can be updated after creation. |\n| `message` | `string` | The human-readable message. This is mutable. |\n| `severity` | `DiagnosticSeverity` | The severity (Error, Warning, Information, Hint). Default is Error. This is mutable. |\n| `source?` | `string` | Optional. A human-readable string describing the source of this diagnostic, e.g., 'typescript', 'eslint', 'super lint'. Shown in the UI to help users identify the diagnostic source. |\n| `code?` | `string \\| number \\| { value: string \\| number; target: Uri }` | Optional. A code or identifier for this diagnostic. When used in code actions, this code can be referenced via `CodeActionContext.diagnostics`. Can be a simple value or an object with a target URI for linking to more information. |\n| `relatedInformation?` | `DiagnosticRelatedInformation[]` | Optional. An array of related diagnostic information. Used to point to code locations that cause or relate to this diagnostic, e.g., when symbol names collide in a scope. |\n| `tags?` | `DiagnosticTag[]` | Optional. Additional metadata tags (e.g., Unnecessary, Deprecated) that influence how the diagnostic is rendered in the editor. |\n\n#### Behavior Notes\n\n- **Immutability of returned diagnostics**: When retrieving diagnostics via `DiagnosticCollection.get()`, the returned array is immutable and cannot be modified. To change diagnostics, you must call `set()` again.\n- **Range precision**: The range determines exact visual highlighting. Small ranges highlight specific tokens; large ranges highlight entire sections.\n- **Severity ordering**: The editor prioritizes display based on severity (Error > Warning > Information > Hint). With very large diagnostic counts, less severe diagnostics may be hidden.\n- **Code linking**: If `code` is an object with a `target` URI, users can click it to navigate to more information, typically in extension documentation or web pages.\n\n#### Example\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nconst range = new vscode.Range(\n  new vscode.Position(0, 0),\n  new vscode.Position(0, 5)\n);\nconst diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n  range,\n  'Unused variable',\n  vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning\n);\ndiagnostic.source = 'eslint';\ndiagnostic.code = 'no-unused-vars';\ndiagnostic.tags = [vscode.DiagnosticTag.Unnecessary];\n```\n\n---\n\n### DiagnosticCollection\n\n**Interface** that acts as a container for managing diagnostics across documents. It provides methods to set, retrieve, and manage diagnostics keyed by URI.\n\n#### Constructor\n\n`DiagnosticCollection` cannot be instantiated directly. Instead, use `languages.createDiagnosticCollection()`.\n\n#### Properties\n\n| Property | Type | Description |\n|----------|------|-------------|\n| `name` | `string` (readonly) | The name of this collection. Every diagnostic from this collection is associated with this name. Used by the task framework for problem matcher integration. Examples: 'typescript', 'eslint', 'myLinter'. |\n\n#### Methods\n\n##### `set(uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined): void`\n\nAssign diagnostics for a given resource, replacing any existing diagnostics for that resource.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri: Uri` - The resource identifier (file path).\n- `diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined` - Array of diagnostics, or `undefined` to clear all diagnostics for this URI.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Passing `undefined` is equivalent to calling `delete(uri)`.\n- Multiple calls to `set()` with the same URI will replace all previous diagnostics for that URI.\n- Diagnostics are stored immutably; the array is copied internally.\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n  range,\n  'Error message',\n  vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n);\ncollection.set(document.uri, [diagnostic]);\n\n// Clear diagnostics for this file\ncollection.set(document.uri, undefined);\n```\n\n##### `set(entries: ReadonlyArray<[Uri, readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined]>): void`\n\nReplace diagnostics for multiple resources in a single call.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `entries` - An array of `[Uri, Diagnostic[]]` tuples.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Multiple tuples with the same URI are merged (combined), e.g., `[[file1, [d1]], [file1, [d2]]]` becomes `[[file1, [d1, d2]]]`.\n- If an entry has `undefined` as diagnostics, all previous diagnostics for that URI are removed (but later entries for the same URI are still processed).\n- This is more efficient than multiple `set()` calls when updating many files.\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst entries: [vscode.Uri, vscode.Diagnostic[]][] = [\n  [file1Uri, [diag1, diag2]],\n  [file2Uri, [diag3]],\n  [file3Uri, undefined] // Clear file3\n];\ncollection.set(entries);\n```\n\n##### `delete(uri: Uri): void`\n\nRemove all diagnostics for a given resource.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri: Uri` - The resource identifier.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Equivalent to calling `set(uri, undefined)`.\n- Does nothing if the URI has no diagnostics.\n\n##### `clear(): void`\n\nRemove all diagnostics from this collection across all resources.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Fires the `onDidChangeDiagnostics` event with all affected URIs.\n\n##### `forEach(callback: (uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[], collection: DiagnosticCollection) => any, thisArg?: any): void`\n\nIterate over each entry in the collection.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `callback` - Function called for each URI/diagnostics pair.\n- `thisArg` - Optional `this` context for the callback.\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\ncollection.forEach((uri, diagnostics, col) => {\n  console.log(`${uri.path}: ${diagnostics.length} diagnostics`);\n});\n```\n\n##### `get(uri: Uri): readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined`\n\nGet the diagnostics for a given resource.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri: Uri` - The resource identifier.\n\n**Returns:**\n- An immutable array of diagnostics, or `undefined` if the URI has no diagnostics.\n\n**Important:** The returned array is immutable and cannot be modified. To update diagnostics, call `set()` with a new array.\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnostics = collection.get(document.uri);\nif (diagnostics) {\n  console.log(`Found ${diagnostics.length} diagnostics`);\n}\n```\n\n##### `has(uri: Uri): boolean`\n\nCheck if this collection contains diagnostics for a given resource.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri: Uri` - The resource identifier.\n\n**Returns:**\n- `true` if the collection has any diagnostics for the URI, `false` otherwise.\n\n##### `dispose(): void`\n\nDispose and free associated resources. Clears all diagnostics from the collection.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Calls `clear()` internally.\n- The collection becomes unusable after disposal.\n- Typically called during extension deactivation.\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('myLinter');\n// ... use collection ...\ncollection.dispose(); // Clean up on extension deactivation\n```\n\n#### Iterable Support\n\n`DiagnosticCollection` implements `Iterable<[uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[]]>`, allowing it to be used with `for...of`:\n\n```typescript\nfor (const [uri, diagnostics] of collection) {\n  console.log(`${uri.path}: ${diagnostics.length} issues`);\n}\n```\n\n#### Behavior Notes\n\n- **Cardinality limits**: VS Code has a maximum of 1000 diagnostics per file. If more are provided, only the highest-severity diagnostics are kept, with lower-severity diagnostics removed. The global limit is approximately 1100 diagnostics per file across all collections.\n- **Immutability**: Once a diagnostic array is set, the internal copy is immutable. Modifying the original array after calling `set()` has no effect.\n- **URI equivalence**: URIs are compared by their string representation. URIs with identical components but different representations may be treated as different.\n\n---\n\n### DiagnosticSeverity\n\n**Enum** that defines the severity levels for diagnostics.\n\n```typescript\nexport enum DiagnosticSeverity {\n  Error = 0,\n  Warning = 1,\n  Information = 2,\n  Hint = 3\n}\n```\n\n#### Members\n\n| Member | Value | Description |\n|--------|-------|-------------|\n| `Error` | `0` | Something not allowed by the rules of a language or other means. Shown with red squiggle. Highest priority. |\n| `Warning` | `1` | Something suspicious but allowed. Shown with orange/yellow squiggle. |\n| `Information` | `2` | Something to inform about but not a problem. Shown with blue squiggle. |\n| `Hint` | `3` | Something to hint at a better way of doing it, like proposing a refactoring. Shown with green squiggle or lightbulb. Lowest priority. |\n\n#### Usage Notes\n\n- **Default severity**: If not specified, `Diagnostic` defaults to `Error`.\n- **Display priority**: When the editor has space constraints, higher-severity diagnostics are shown first.\n- **Visual rendering**: Each severity has associated colors configured via VS Code's theme.\n\n#### Example\n```typescript\nconst errorDiag = new vscode.Diagnostic(range, 'Critical error', vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error);\nconst warnDiag = new vscode.Diagnostic(range, 'Potential issue', vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning);\nconst infoDiag = new vscode.Diagnostic(range, 'FYI', vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Information);\nconst hintDiag = new vscode.Diagnostic(range, 'Try this instead', vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Hint);\n```\n\n---\n\n### DiagnosticRelatedInformation\n\n**Class** representing additional context for a diagnostic, pointing to related code locations.\n\n#### Constructor\n```typescript\nnew DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n  location: Location,\n  message: string\n)\n```\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `location: Location` - **Required**. The location in code that relates to the diagnostic. Includes both a URI and a range.\n- `message: string` - **Required**. A human-readable message describing the relationship.\n\n#### Properties\n\n| Property | Type | Description |\n|----------|------|-------------|\n| `location` | `Location` | The location (URI + range) of this related information. |\n| `message` | `string` | A human-readable message explaining the relationship. |\n\n#### Use Cases\n\n- **Duplicate symbols**: When a symbol name collides in a scope, mark all definitions.\n- **Multi-location issues**: Point to multiple locations that together form a problem.\n- **Related errors**: Show related errors or warnings in other files.\n\n#### Example\n```typescript\nconst diag = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n  range,\n  'Duplicate symbol name',\n  vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n);\n\n// Link to the first occurrence of the symbol\ndiag.relatedInformation = [\n  new vscode.DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n    new vscode.Location(file1Uri, otherRange),\n    'First defined here'\n  ),\n  new vscode.DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n    new vscode.Location(file2Uri, anotherRange),\n    'Also defined here'\n  )\n];\n```\n\n#### Behavior Notes\n\n- **UI rendering**: VS Code displays related information as links in the Problems panel and hover tooltips.\n- **Navigation**: Clicking a related information link navigates to that location.\n\n---\n\n### DiagnosticTag\n\n**Enum** providing metadata about diagnostic types that influence rendering.\n\n```typescript\nexport enum DiagnosticTag {\n  Unnecessary = 1,\n  Deprecated = 2\n}\n```\n\n#### Members\n\n| Member | Value | Description |\n|--------|-------|-------------|\n| `Unnecessary` | `1` | Marks unused or unnecessary code. Rendered faded out (opacity controlled by `editorUnnecessaryCode.opacity` theme color). In high-contrast themes, uses `editorUnnecessaryCode.border` to underline instead. |\n| `Deprecated` | `2` | Marks deprecated or obsolete code. Rendered with a strike-through effect. |\n\n#### Theme Color Configuration\n\n**For `Unnecessary` tag:**\n```json\n{\n  \"editorUnnecessaryCode.opacity\": \"#000000c0\",  // 75% opacity\n  \"editorUnnecessaryCode.border\": \"#ff0000\"      // Red underline in high contrast\n}\n```\n\n#### Usage Notes\n\n- **Visual feedback**: Tags provide visual cues beyond severity color. Multiple tags can be applied to a single diagnostic.\n- **User intent**: These tags communicate intent more precisely than severity alone (e.g., a warning about unused code is more specific than generic warning).\n\n#### Example\n```typescript\nconst diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n  range,\n  'Unused variable `x`',\n  vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Information\n);\ndiagnostic.tags = [vscode.DiagnosticTag.Unnecessary];\n\nconst deprecated = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n  range,\n  'This API is deprecated',\n  vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning\n);\ndeprecated.tags = [vscode.DiagnosticTag.Deprecated];\n```\n\n---\n\n## Functions\n\n### createDiagnosticCollection()\n\nFactory function to create a new `DiagnosticCollection`.\n\n#### Signature\n```typescript\nexport function createDiagnosticCollection(name?: string): DiagnosticCollection\n```\n\n#### Parameters\n\n- `name?: string` - **Optional**. The name of the collection. If not provided, a unique auto-generated name is used. The name is associated with all diagnostics in the collection and is used by the task framework for problem matcher integration.\n\n#### Returns\n\nA new `DiagnosticCollection` instance.\n\n#### Behavior Notes\n\n- **Ownership**: The returned collection is owned by the extension. The extension is responsible for populating and disposing of it.\n- **Uniqueness**: Each call returns a new, independent collection. Collections with the same name are distinct objects.\n- **Task framework integration**: If you want problem matchers to recognize your diagnostics, use a consistent name (e.g., 'myLinter', 'typescript').\n- **Resource lifecycle**: The collection persists until explicitly disposed.\n\n#### Example\n```typescript\nconst collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('myLinter');\n\n// Later, set diagnostics\nconst diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(range, 'Issue found');\ncollection.set(document.uri, [diagnostic]);\n\n// On deactivation, clean up\nvscode.workspace.onDidChangeConfiguration(() => {\n  collection.clear();\n});\n\n// In extension deactivate()\nexport function deactivate() {\n  collection.dispose();\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### getDiagnostics()\n\nRetrieve diagnostics from the workspace.\n\n#### Overload 1: Get diagnostics for a specific resource\n```typescript\nexport function getDiagnostics(resource: Uri): Diagnostic[]\n```\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `resource: Uri` - The resource (file path) to get diagnostics for.\n\n**Returns:**\n- An array of all diagnostics for that resource across all collections, or an empty array if none.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns diagnostics from all diagnostic collections (both built-in and extension-created).\n- Does not include only the diagnostics from a single collection; this is a global query.\n\n#### Overload 2: Get all diagnostics\n```typescript\nexport function getDiagnostics(): [Uri, Diagnostic[]][]\n```\n\n**Parameters:** None\n\n**Returns:**\n- An array of `[Uri, Diagnostic[]]` tuples representing all diagnostics in the workspace across all collections.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns a snapshot of diagnostics at the time of the call.\n- Does not include URIs with zero diagnostics.\n\n#### Example\n```typescript\n// Get diagnostics for a specific file\nconst fileDiags = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(document.uri);\nconsole.log(`File has ${fileDiags.length} diagnostics`);\n\n// Get all diagnostics in the workspace\nconst allDiags = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics();\nlet totalDiagCount = 0;\nfor (const [uri, diags] of allDiags) {\n  console.log(`${uri.path}: ${diags.length}`);\n  totalDiagCount += diags.length;\n}\nconsole.log(`Total: ${totalDiagCount}`);\n```\n\n#### Behavior Notes\n\n- **Aggregation**: Results include diagnostics from all sources (language servers, linters, type checkers, etc.).\n- **Immutability**: The returned arrays are read-only and cannot be modified.\n- **Performance**: Retrieving all diagnostics in a large workspace can be expensive. Filter by URI when possible.\n\n---\n\n## Events\n\n### onDidChangeDiagnostics\n\n**Event** fired when the global set of diagnostics changes (new or removed diagnostics).\n\n#### Signature\n```typescript\nexport const onDidChangeDiagnostics: Event<DiagnosticChangeEvent>\n```\n\n#### DiagnosticChangeEvent Interface\n```typescript\nexport interface DiagnosticChangeEvent {\n  readonly uris: readonly Uri[];\n}\n```\n\n**Properties:**\n- `uris: readonly Uri[]` - An array of URIs for which diagnostics have changed (either added, modified, or removed).\n\n#### Subscription\n```typescript\nexport interface Event<T> {\n  (listener: (e: T) => any, thisArgs?: any, disposables?: Disposable[]): Disposable\n}\n```\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `listener` - Callback function invoked when diagnostics change.\n- `thisArgs` - Optional `this` context for the callback.\n- `disposables` - Optional array to which an unsubscribe disposable will be added.\n\n**Returns:** A `Disposable` that unsubscribes the listener when disposed.\n\n#### When the Event Fires\n\n- When any extension's `DiagnosticCollection.set()` is called.\n- When an extension's collection is `clear()`d or `dispose()`d.\n- When a collection's diagnostics are replaced with `set(entries)`.\n- When a specific resource's diagnostics are `delete()`d.\n\n#### Important Notes\n\n- **Batching**: The event may be debounced (delayed) if many changes occur in quick succession, batching them together for efficiency.\n- **URI list only**: The event provides the list of changed URIs but not the actual diagnostics. To inspect diagnostics, call `getDiagnostics()`.\n- **Performance**: Do not perform expensive operations directly in the listener; schedule async work instead.\n\n#### Example\n```typescript\nconst disposable = vscode.languages.onDidChangeDiagnostics((event) => {\n  console.log(`Diagnostics changed for ${event.uris.length} URIs`);\n\n  for (const uri of event.uris) {\n    const diags = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(uri);\n    console.log(`${uri.path}: ${diags.length} diagnostics`);\n\n    // Filter and process\n    const errors = diags.filter(d => d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error);\n    console.log(`  Errors: ${errors.length}`);\n  }\n});\n\n// Later, unsubscribe\ndisposable.dispose();\n```\n\n#### Cleanup\n\nThe listener is automatically cleaned up when:\n1. The returned `Disposable` is disposed.\n2. The extension is deactivated.\n\nIt's good practice to return the disposable from `activate()` or add it to a disposables list:\n```typescript\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n  context.subscriptions.push(\n    vscode.languages.onDidChangeDiagnostics(handler)\n  );\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Usage Examples\n\n### Basic Example: Creating and Publishing Diagnostics\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n  // Create a diagnostic collection\n  const diagnostics = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('myLinter');\n  context.subscriptions.push(diagnostics);\n\n  // Listen for text document changes\n  vscode.workspace.onDidOpenTextDocument((document) => {\n    lintDocument(document, diagnostics);\n  });\n\n  vscode.workspace.onDidChangeTextDocument((event) => {\n    lintDocument(event.document, diagnostics);\n  });\n\n  vscode.workspace.onDidCloseTextDocument((document) => {\n    // Clear diagnostics when document is closed\n    diagnostics.delete(document.uri);\n  });\n\n  // Lint existing documents\n  vscode.workspace.textDocuments.forEach((document) => {\n    lintDocument(document, diagnostics);\n  });\n}\n\nfunction lintDocument(\n  document: vscode.TextDocument,\n  diagnostics: vscode.DiagnosticCollection\n) {\n  const issues: vscode.Diagnostic[] = [];\n\n  // Simple example: flag lines longer than 120 characters\n  for (let i = 0; i < document.lineCount; i++) {\n    const line = document.lineAt(i);\n    if (line.text.length > 120) {\n      const range = new vscode.Range(\n        new vscode.Position(i, 120),\n        new vscode.Position(i, line.text.length)\n      );\n      const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n        range,\n        'Line exceeds 120 characters',\n        vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning\n      );\n      diagnostic.source = 'myLinter';\n      diagnostic.code = 'line-length';\n      issues.push(diagnostic);\n    }\n  }\n\n  // Publish all diagnostics for this document\n  diagnostics.set(document.uri, issues);\n}\n\nexport function deactivate() {\n  // Clean up is handled by context.subscriptions\n}\n```\n\n### Advanced Example: Multiple Files with Related Information\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n  const diagnostics = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('analyzer');\n  context.subscriptions.push(diagnostics);\n\n  const analyzeWorkspace = async () => {\n    // Find all duplicate symbol definitions\n    const allSymbols = await findAllSymbols();\n    const duplicates = findDuplicates(allSymbols);\n\n    // Create diagnostics for each duplicate\n    const entries: [vscode.Uri, vscode.Diagnostic[]][] = [];\n\n    for (const [symbolName, locations] of duplicates) {\n      for (let i = 0; i < locations.length; i++) {\n        const location = locations[i];\n        const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n          location.range,\n          `Duplicate symbol: '${symbolName}' is defined ${locations.length} times`,\n          vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n        );\n        diagnostic.source = 'analyzer';\n        diagnostic.code = { value: 'duplicate-symbol', target: vscode.Uri.parse('https://docs.example.com/rules/duplicate-symbol') };\n\n        // Link to all other definitions\n        diagnostic.relatedInformation = locations\n          .map((loc, idx) => idx !== i ? loc : null)\n          .filter(Boolean)\n          .map((loc) => new vscode.DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n            loc,\n            `Other definition of '${symbolName}'`\n          ));\n\n        entries.push([location.uri, [diagnostic]]);\n      }\n    }\n\n    // Set all diagnostics at once\n    diagnostics.set(entries);\n  };\n\n  // Re-analyze when configuration changes\n  context.subscriptions.push(\n    vscode.workspace.onDidChangeConfiguration(() => {\n      analyzeWorkspace();\n    })\n  );\n\n  // Initial analysis\n  analyzeWorkspace();\n}\n\nasync function findAllSymbols(): Promise<Map<string, vscode.Location[]>> {\n  // Implementation omitted\n  return new Map();\n}\n\nfunction findDuplicates(\n  symbols: Map<string, vscode.Location[]>\n): Map<string, vscode.Location[]> {\n  const duplicates = new Map<string, vscode.Location[]>();\n  for (const [name, locations] of symbols) {\n    if (locations.length > 1) {\n      duplicates.set(name, locations);\n    }\n  }\n  return duplicates;\n}\n```\n\n### Example: Monitoring Diagnostic Changes\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n  // Monitor when diagnostics change globally\n  const listener = vscode.languages.onDidChangeDiagnostics((event) => {\n    console.log('Diagnostics changed!');\n    console.log(`Modified URIs: ${event.uris.length}`);\n\n    // Count errors and warnings\n    let totalErrors = 0;\n    let totalWarnings = 0;\n\n    for (const uri of event.uris) {\n      const diags = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(uri);\n      for (const diag of diags) {\n        if (diag.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error) {\n          totalErrors++;\n        } else if (diag.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning) {\n          totalWarnings++;\n        }\n      }\n    }\n\n    console.log(`Total errors: ${totalErrors}, warnings: ${totalWarnings}`);\n\n    // Update status bar\n    if (totalErrors > 0) {\n      vscode.window.setStatusBarMessage(`$(error) ${totalErrors} errors`);\n    } else if (totalWarnings > 0) {\n      vscode.window.setStatusBarMessage(`$(warning) ${totalWarnings} warnings`);\n    }\n  });\n\n  context.subscriptions.push(listener);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Common Patterns\n\n### Pattern 1: Batch Updating Multiple Files\n\nInstead of calling `set()` multiple times, batch updates for better performance:\n\n```typescript\n// ❌ Inefficient: Multiple calls\ndiagnostics.set(file1, diags1);\ndiagnostics.set(file2, diags2);\ndiagnostics.set(file3, diags3);\n\n// ✅ Efficient: Batch call\ndiagnostics.set([\n  [file1, diags1],\n  [file2, diags2],\n  [file3, diags3],\n]);\n```\n\n### Pattern 2: Clearing Diagnostics\n\n```typescript\n// Option 1: Clear specific file\ndiagnostics.delete(uri);\n\n// Option 2: Clear all with undefined\ndiagnostics.set(uri, undefined);\n\n// Option 3: Clear entire collection\ndiagnostics.clear();\n```\n\n### Pattern 3: Code Actions Linked to Diagnostics\n\nUse the `code` property to connect diagnostics to code actions:\n\n```typescript\n// In your linter\nconst diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(range, 'Use const instead of let');\ndiagnostic.code = { value: 'prefer-const', target: vscode.Uri.parse('https://...') };\n\n// In your code action provider\nvscode.languages.registerCodeActionProvider('javascript', {\n  provideCodeActions(document, range, context) {\n    return context.diagnostics\n      .filter(d => d.code?.value === 'prefer-const')\n      .map(d => {\n        const action = new vscode.CodeAction('Use const', vscode.CodeActionKind.QuickFix);\n        action.edit = new vscode.WorkspaceEdit();\n        action.edit.replace(document.uri, d.range, 'const');\n        return action;\n      });\n  }\n});\n```\n\n### Pattern 4: Filtering and Querying Diagnostics\n\n```typescript\n// Get all errors in current document\nconst errors = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(editor.document.uri)\n  .filter(d => d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error);\n\n// Get all diagnostics from a specific source\nconst tsDiagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics()\n  .flatMap(([uri, diags]) => diags.filter(d => d.source === 'typescript'))\n  .map(d => d);\n\n// Count diagnostics by severity\nconst summary = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics().reduce(\n  (acc, [_uri, diags]) => {\n    for (const d of diags) {\n      acc[d.severity] = (acc[d.severity] || 0) + 1;\n    }\n    return acc;\n  },\n  {} as Record<number, number>\n);\n```\n\n### Pattern 5: Document-Scoped Diagnostics\n\nIf your extension only cares about the active document:\n\n```typescript\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n  const diagnostics = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('myLinter');\n  context.subscriptions.push(diagnostics);\n\n  let lastDocument: vscode.TextDocument | undefined;\n\n  const lint = (document: vscode.TextDocument) => {\n    if (lastDocument && lastDocument !== document) {\n      // Clear diagnostics from the previous document\n      diagnostics.delete(lastDocument.uri);\n    }\n    lastDocument = document;\n\n    const issues = performLinting(document);\n    diagnostics.set(document.uri, issues);\n  };\n\n  if (vscode.window.activeTextEditor) {\n    lint(vscode.window.activeTextEditor.document);\n  }\n\n  context.subscriptions.push(\n    vscode.window.onDidChangeActiveTextEditor((editor) => {\n      if (editor) lint(editor.document);\n    }),\n    vscode.workspace.onDidChangeTextDocument((event) => {\n      if (event.document === vscode.window.activeTextEditor?.document) {\n        lint(event.document);\n      }\n    })\n  );\n}\n\nfunction performLinting(document: vscode.TextDocument): vscode.Diagnostic[] {\n  // Your linting logic here\n  return [];\n}\n```\n\n### Pattern 6: Debouncing Diagnostic Updates\n\nFor performance, debounce frequent updates:\n\n```typescript\nimport { throttle } from 'lodash'; // or implement your own\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n  const diagnostics = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('myLinter');\n  context.subscriptions.push(diagnostics);\n\n  const debouncedLint = throttle((document: vscode.TextDocument) => {\n    const issues = performLinting(document);\n    diagnostics.set(document.uri, issues);\n  }, 500); // Update at most every 500ms\n\n  context.subscriptions.push(\n    vscode.workspace.onDidChangeTextDocument((event) => {\n      debouncedLint(event.document);\n    })\n  );\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Common Error Scenarios\n\n#### 1. Setting Diagnostics on Non-Existent URI\n\n```typescript\n// This doesn't cause an error, but the diagnostics are stored\n// and will appear if the file is ever opened\ndiagnostics.set(vscode.Uri.parse('file:///does/not/exist.js'), [diagnostic]);\n```\n\n#### 2. Disposed Collection\n\nAttempting to use a disposed `DiagnosticCollection` throws an error:\n\n```typescript\nconst col = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('test');\ncol.dispose();\n\ncol.set(uri, [diagnostic]); // ❌ Throws: Collection is disposed\n```\n\n**Prevention:**\n```typescript\nconst disposables: vscode.Disposable[] = [];\nconst col = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('test');\ndisposables.push(col);\n\nexport function deactivate() {\n  disposables.forEach(d => d.dispose());\n}\n```\n\n#### 3. Modifying Returned Diagnostic Array\n\n```typescript\nconst diags = collection.get(uri); // Returns immutable array\ndiags[0].message = 'New message'; // ❌ Change is not reflected\n\n// ✅ Correct approach:\nconst updated = diags.map(d => {\n  if (d === diags[0]) {\n    const newDiag = new vscode.Diagnostic(d.range, 'New message', d.severity);\n    newDiag.source = d.source;\n    return newDiag;\n  }\n  return d;\n});\ncollection.set(uri, updated);\n```\n\n#### 4. Diagnostic Count Limits\n\nVS Code limits diagnostics per file to prevent performance degradation:\n\n```typescript\n// If you set more than ~1000 diagnostics per file,\n// only the highest-severity ones are retained\nconst tooMany = Array.from({ length: 2000 }, (_, i) =>\n  new vscode.Diagnostic(\n    new vscode.Range(i, 0, i, 1),\n    'Issue',\n    vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Hint\n  )\n);\n\ndiagnostics.set(uri, tooMany); // Only ~1000 stored (highest severity prioritized)\n```\n\n**Best practice:** Don't generate excessive diagnostics. Consider aggregating or sampling them.\n\n#### 5. Missing Required Properties\n\n```typescript\n// ❌ Invalid: missing range\nconst bad = new vscode.Diagnostic(null, 'message'); // TypeScript error\n\n// ❌ Invalid: missing message\nconst bad2 = new vscode.Diagnostic(range, ''); // Empty string is allowed but not useful\n\n// ✅ Valid: minimal required properties\nconst good = new vscode.Diagnostic(range, 'message');\n```\n\n### Defensive Programming Practices\n\n```typescript\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n  const diagnostics = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('myLinter');\n  context.subscriptions.push(diagnostics);\n\n  const safeLint = async (document: vscode.TextDocument) => {\n    try {\n      if (!document.uri.fsPath.endsWith('.myLang')) {\n        return; // Skip non-relevant files\n      }\n\n      const issues = await performLinting(document);\n\n      // Validate diagnostics before setting\n      const valid = issues.filter(d => {\n        if (!d.range || !d.message) {\n          console.warn('Invalid diagnostic, skipping:', d);\n          return false;\n        }\n        return true;\n      });\n\n      diagnostics.set(document.uri, valid);\n    } catch (error) {\n      console.error('Linting failed:', error);\n      // Optionally set an error diagnostic\n      const errorDiag = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n        new vscode.Range(0, 0, 0, 0),\n        `Linting error: ${String(error)}`,\n        vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n      );\n      diagnostics.set(document.uri, [errorDiag]);\n    }\n  };\n\n  context.subscriptions.push(\n    vscode.workspace.onDidChangeTextDocument((event) => {\n      safeLint(event.document).catch(console.error);\n    })\n  );\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Real-World Patterns from VS Code Extensions\n\n### Pattern from TypeScript Extension\n\nThe TypeScript extension maps TypeScript diagnostics to VS Code diagnostics, preserving diagnostic codes and related information:\n\n```typescript\nconst typeScriptDiagnostic = serverDiagnostic;\nconst vscDiagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n  serverDiagnostic.range,\n  serverDiagnostic.message,\n  mapSeverity(serverDiagnostic.category)\n);\nvscDiagnostic.source = 'typescript';\nvscDiagnostic.code = serverDiagnostic.code;\n\nif (serverDiagnostic.relatedInformation) {\n  vscDiagnostic.relatedInformation = serverDiagnostic.relatedInformation\n    .map(info => new vscode.DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n      new vscode.Location(info.file, info.range),\n      info.message\n    ));\n}\n```\n\n### Pattern from Extension-Editing Extension\n\nThe built-in Extension Editing extension validates `package.json` files and uses diagnostic codes with links:\n\n```typescript\nconst diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n  range,\n  'Unsafe activation event',\n  vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n);\ndiagnostic.code = {\n  value: 'unsafe-activation-event',\n  target: vscode.Uri.parse('https://code.visualstudio.com/api/references/activation-events')\n};\n```\n\nThis pattern allows users to click the diagnostic code to learn more.\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe VS Code Diagnostic API provides a robust system for reporting code issues to users. Key takeaways:\n\n1. **Collections** organize diagnostics and associate them with a source name.\n2. **Severity** determines visual priority and how diagnostics are displayed.\n3. **Related information** provides additional context by linking to related code locations.\n4. **Tags** (Unnecessary, Deprecated) provide visual and semantic hints about diagnostic types.\n5. **Events** allow extensions to react to diagnostic changes globally.\n6. **Batch operations** improve performance when updating many files.\n7. **Proper cleanup** via `dispose()` is essential for extension health.\n\nUse this API to provide timely, contextual feedback to developers about code quality, style, and correctness issues within VS Code.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
